  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_c9c1c85b-b661-4ece-b02f-7a7815fc352b'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer4561026320361433954">Komarr could be a garden with a thousand more years' work, or an uninhabitable wasteland if the terraforming fails. Now, the solar mirror vital to the terraforming of the conquered planet has been shattered by a ship hurtling off course. The Emperor of Barrayar sends his newest imperial auditor, Lord Miles Vorkosigan, to find out why. The choice is not a popular one on Kom</span>
  <span id="freeText4561026320361433954" style="display:none">Komarr could be a garden with a thousand more years' work, or an uninhabitable wasteland if the terraforming fails. Now, the solar mirror vital to the terraforming of the conquered planet has been shattered by a ship hurtling off course. The Emperor of Barrayar sends his newest imperial auditor, Lord Miles Vorkosigan, to find out why. The choice is not a popular one on Komarr, where a betrayal a generation before drenched the name of Vorkosigan in blood. Thus, the Komarrans surrounding Miles could be loyal subjects, potential hostages, innocent victims, or rebels ready for revenge. Lies within lies, treachery within treachery, Miles is caught in a race against time to stop a plot that could exile him from Barrayar forever. His burning hope lies in an unexpected ally, one with wounds as deep and honor as beleaguered as his own.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4561026320361433954" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1965597217" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1965597217" />
    <a title="Evgeny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny"><img alt="Evgeny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544797852p2/9340136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1965597217?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgeny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgeny" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9340136-evgeny?shelf=scifi">scifi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1965597217" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3588605455281413605"><b>A buddy read with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/27962805-choko' rel='nofollow noopener'>Choko</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/15922517-maria-dimitrova' rel='nofollow noopener'>Maria</a>.</b><br/><br/>My biggest and constant complaint about the series is its predictability. Let me demonstrate it on this example. The previous book left Miles being a junior guy in a very important job. His seniors mentioned junior guys get the most troublesome job in the most troublesome place. What would be the most troublesome place for Miles in the whole Empire? Planet Komarr where people believe his father was responsible for a grand massacre and regarded Miles accordingly.</span>
  <span id="freeText3588605455281413605" style="display:none"><b>A buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/27962805-choko" rel="nofollow noopener">Choko</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/15922517-maria-dimitrova" rel="nofollow noopener">Maria</a>.</b><br><br>My biggest and constant complaint about the series is its predictability. Let me demonstrate it on this example. The previous book left Miles being a junior guy in a very important job. His seniors mentioned junior guys get the most troublesome job in the most troublesome place. What would be the most troublesome place for Miles in the whole Empire? Planet Komarr where people believe his father was responsible for a grand massacre and regarded Miles accordingly. <br><br>Also in the previous book Miles parted ways with his girlfriend. It follows he was supposed to find his love interest. And thus I just gave away the whole plot of this book: Miles had to go to Komarr to do his job where he met a woman he fell in love with. All this info can be gathered from the simple fact that the previous book, Memory has a sequel. <br><br>I already mentioned the good parts in my review of practically all books of the series: great writing, interesting plot, some occasional humor. All of these apply here and bring the rating to 4 stars. Why not 5?<br><br>Here come my personal nitpicking. Miles love, Ekaterin is not a woman to make him shine. Quinn was excellent and so was Taura (don't ask). Ekaterin comes across as a timid creature totally beaten into complete submission by her loser husband - in other words exactly the opposite of Miles. <br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1493339209i/22605525._SX540_.jpg" width="460" height="230" alt="Abused wife" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>For this reason their attraction feels artificial. I will stop here as I have another chance to talk about Miles' love in my review for the next book. <br><br>I loved space opera type adventures of Miles. His ground political play is good, but not quite on the same level of excitement: good, but not great. Compare this:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1493339494i/22605541._SX540_.jpg" width="460" height="300" alt="Space battle" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>and this:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1493339364i/22605536._SX540_.jpg" width="460" height="300" alt="Politicians" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I think I made my point. <br><br>These two reasons resulted in one less star of a perfect rating. 4 stars still mean the book is very good though. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3588605455281413605" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1874231595" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1874231595" />
    <a title="Choko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27962805-choko"><img alt="Choko" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475642755p2/27962805.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1874231595?book_show_action=true">Apr 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Choko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Choko" href="/user/show/27962805-choko">Choko</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=sci-fi-fantasy">sci-fi-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1874231595" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer218697972077986084"><b>*** 4.35 ***<br/><br/>A buddy read with Evgeny and Maria, because we cannot stop the Forward Momentum!!! </b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>"...“All the geniuses I ever met were so just part of the time. To qualify, you only have to be great once, you know. Once when it matters.” ..."</i>
</b><br/><br/>Once again I am going to sound like a fan-girl, but I can't help it! This series has stolen my heart. I know I have several series of books which I love and are a must read for me, but most of them are more because the story lines are not finished, and the</span>
  <span id="freeText218697972077986084" style="display:none"><b>*** 4.35 ***<br /><br />A buddy read with Evgeny and Maria, because we cannot stop the Forward Momentum!!! </b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>"...“All the geniuses I ever met were so just part of the time. To qualify, you only have to be great once, you know. Once when it matters.” ..."</i>
</b><br /><br />Once again I am going to sound like a fan-girl, but I can't help it! This series has stolen my heart. I know I have several series of books which I love and are a must read for me, but most of them are more because the story lines are not finished, and the worlds are marvelous, and the writing is great, and I really enjoy the characters... and so on. However, of all of those, The Vorkosigan Saga is the one that I have the most tenderness for. It makes me think, it makes me feel, and it makes me appreciate the more imperfect of the human emotions, the issues we are dealing with in one way or another on daily basis but disguised in a Sci-Fi form. On top of that, as the main protagonist we have Miles, a young man whom we have followed for several years and his evolution form a kid to an adult has been spellbinding... I fill like he is my kid, or more correctly, as if he is my sister's kid and I get to claim and be proud of him and his achievements even though I have been just an observer in his life... He is bigger than life, but packed in a small frame and vulnerable psyche. I love this character so much, he is quickly becoming one of my favorite of all time! <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"...“Some people grow into their dreams, instead of out of them.” ..."</i>
</b><br /><br />This is the first book since he had to part with his second personality, Admiral Naismith, and is now just Lord Vorkosigan, the Imperial auditor. A position which would be the professional peak of any other person on Barrayar, is just "settling" for our Miles... It has been 3 months since he took this post and he is learning on the job by assisting a senior member of the Imperial Auditors. They have to investigate what happened on Komarr, a planet which Miles's father was instrumental in conquering and at the time acquiring the nickname "The Butcher of Komarr"... Having his son on the planet is a bit challenging for the locals, to put it mildly... On top of that, they are staying with the niece of the older partner and her family, which are having some domestic problems and there are multiple tensions in the air. Incidentally, the niece, Ekaterin, happens to be just Miles's type and very unhappy in her marriage... Tum-tum-tuuuummmm.... (there was no cheating, for which I was very grateful!!!) <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"...“So the difference between a criminal and a hero is the order in which their vile crimes are committed. And justice comes with a sell-by date. In that case, you’d better hurry. You wouldn't want your heroism to spoil.” ..."</i>
</b><br /><br />As always, we get the usual action, political machinations, and the mandatory ethical conundrum, mostly based on genetic mutations and conditions. The good thing is, this world is fictional and things can get fixed, while we don't have those luxuries in RL:(((... I love how the author handles all of those situations without making them preachy or intrusive. They are looked upon as just a part of human everyday life and we can imagine parents, kids and spouses dealing with them in just this manner... <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"...““He’s not so short,” said Ekaterin defensively. “He’s just . . . concentrated.” ..."</i>
</b><br /><br />As always I would like to encourage all readers to try this series and see if it is something they might like - it is a great series for young and old alike, because there are situations and issues which are thought provoking for those who have no real life experience as well as those who have had more than they would have liked to have had:):):):) <br /><br />I wish you all Happy Reading and many more wonderful books to come!!!! </span>
  <a data-text-id="218697972077986084" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_492471891" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/492471891" />
    <a title="Maria Dimitrova" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15922517-maria-dimitrova"><img alt="Maria Dimitrova" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1563534668p2/15922517.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/492471891?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria Dimitrova" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria Dimitrova" href="/user/show/15922517-maria-dimitrova">Maria Dimitrova</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15922517-maria-dimitrova?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15922517-maria-dimitrova?shelf=barrayar">barrayar</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer492471891" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8938469458246352559"><b>Buddy read with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/27962805-choko' rel='nofollow noopener'>Choko</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/9340136-evgeny' rel='nofollow noopener'>Evgeny</a>.</b><br/><br/>I started writing this review yesterday and then RL happened. Let's hope that nothing will interrupt me this time :)<br/><br/>From the very start of the series the planet Komarr has played an important but kind of behind the scenes role in Vorkosigan's lives. And I always wanted to visit it. Mostly because terraforming fascinates me. It's very difficult to write a good book set on a terraformed planet because it's either used as a convenient plot device and the science is </span>
  <span id="freeText8938469458246352559" style="display:none"><b>Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/27962805-choko" rel="nofollow noopener">Choko</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/9340136-evgeny" rel="nofollow noopener">Evgeny</a>.</b><br /><br />I started writing this review yesterday and then RL happened. Let's hope that nothing will interrupt me this time :)<br /><br />From the very start of the series the planet Komarr has played an important but kind of behind the scenes role in Vorkosigan's lives. And I always wanted to visit it. Mostly because terraforming fascinates me. It's very difficult to write a good book set on a terraformed planet because it's either used as a convenient plot device and the science is so badly researched/explained that it drives me crazy or the technical details are overwhelming and make the reader feel as if she's picked a textbook. LMB has found the perfect balance between those two opposites and blends it seamlessly with the story.<br /><br />For me this is a reread number "I've lost count" and up until now I was always focused on Miles' side of the story. He does tend to hoard all the attention :) But this time it was Ekaterin's POV that kept me going. Maybe it's because I'm older and have seen the destruction a dysfunctional relationship can bring to a person in RL and that's why Ekaterin's plight hit me so hard. I admire her for finding the strength to <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[leave Tien <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> because not many people do. Mostly I love how LMB handled the situation - she made it feel real, something few authors manage to do. The inner struggle Ekaterin went through, the excuses she made for so long, the fear, the pain, the ultimate trigger for her decision - everything was described so well that for a moment I forgot that it isn't real. <br /><br /><i>Komarr</i> fits perfectly with the rest of the series not because Miles is in it but because of Ekaterin. All of the books deal with some sort of social problem and it's sad that those problems are still such a big part of society years after these books were written. And as much as I love Miles and his family it's those themes that make me reread these books time and again. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8938469458246352559" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_349494079" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/349494079" />
    <a title="Clouds" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9374686-clouds"><img alt="Clouds" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514641128p2/9374686.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/349494079?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Clouds" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Clouds" href="/user/show/9374686-clouds">Clouds</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780671017835" href="/book/show/1106502.Komarr">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9374686-clouds?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9374686-clouds?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9374686-clouds?shelf=pub-1990s">pub-1990s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9374686-clouds?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9374686-clouds?shelf=gifts">gifts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9374686-clouds?shelf=vorkosigan-saga">vorkosigan-saga</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer349494079" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4702479664879919917"><a href='http://www.theaceofclouds.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380317319i/689370.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><b>Following the resounding success of my <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/story/show/332414-reading-lists?chapter=2' rel='nofollow noopener'>Locus Quest</a>, I faced a dilemma: which reading list to follow it up with? Variety is the spice of life, so I’ve decided to diversify and pursue six different lists simultaneously. This book falls into my <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/story/show/332414?chapter=7' rel='nofollow noopener'>GIFTS AND GUILTY</a> list.<br/><br/>Regardless of how many books are already queued patiently on my reading list, unexpected gifts and guilt-trips will always see unplanned additions muscling their way in at the front.</b><br/><br/>If you’ve never read any of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16094.Lois_McMaster_Bujold' rel='nofollow noopener'>Bujold</a>’s <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/98254-vorkosigan-saga-chronological' rel='nofollow noopener'>Vorkosigan Sa</a></span>
  <span id="freeText4702479664879919917" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.theaceofclouds.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380317319i/689370.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>Following the resounding success of my <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/story/show/332414-reading-lists?chapter=2" rel="nofollow noopener">Locus Quest</a>, I faced a dilemma: which reading list to follow it up with? Variety is the spice of life, so I’ve decided to diversify and pursue six different lists simultaneously. This book falls into my <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/story/show/332414?chapter=7" rel="nofollow noopener">GIFTS AND GUILTY</a> list.<br><br>Regardless of how many books are already queued patiently on my reading list, unexpected gifts and guilt-trips will always see unplanned additions muscling their way in at the front.</b><br><br>If you’ve never read any of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16094.Lois_McMaster_Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">Bujold</a>’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/98254-vorkosigan-saga-chronological" rel="nofollow noopener">Vorkosigan Saga</a> – what are you waiting for? They’re great! However, I wouldn’t recommend making this your first. It’s not the kind of series you have to start at the beginning (I came in at book nine and loved it) but, to me, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1106502.Komarr" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>
    <i>Komarr</i>
  </b>
</a> has the feel of the middle book in a trilogy, a smaller arc within the bigger series. <br><br>If you’ve read one or two other books in the Vorkosiverse - this is Miles’ first adventure since <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61880.Memory" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>Memory</i>
</a>, where he embarked upon his new career as a Galactic Auditor. He’s kind of like a trouble-shooting detective with the authority of the Emperor. Miles is still settling into his new role, trying to find the balance between effective use and reprehensible misuse of his power. In this case, Miles is called in to investigate a massive space accident that has damaged the planet Komarr’s soletta array (terrorist-with-secret-weapon shenanigans ensue).<br><br>If you’re familiar with the broad path of the series – this is “The one where Miles falls in love.” Miles has been in love before –at the end of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1106502.Komarr" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>
    <i>Komarr</i>
  </b>
</a> he even reels off a list of all the people he’s fallen for in the past. But watching Miles falling in love has never been the main focus before, it’s always been a subplot or distraction – but <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16094.Lois_McMaster_Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">Bujold</a> handles it remarkably well, this isn’t a romance in any conventional fashion.<br><br>Ekaterin is no Quinn, nor is she a Taura - those are the wild girls from Miles’ past I was most fond of. Ekaterin is an unhappily married Vor lady with an eight year old son. She’s living on Komarr (not her home planet) and married to a Barayaran Administrator who is a complete tool, on both a personal and professional level. Miles meets her through the course of his investigation and is slowly bewitched by her. The perspective flip-flops between Miles and Ekaterin throughout the story as he tries to stay focused on his case rather than the dame, and she tries to change her life somehow.<br><br>The twist comes during an accident: her husband is killed and the case breaks. Both aspects of the story pick up the pace before combining in a climax dominated by Ekaterin, not Miles; it’s the last straw for Miles and he is irrevocably smitten. <br><br>My favourite quote came right at the end:<blockquote>
  <i>“She had met the enemy, mastered her moment, hung three hours on death’s doorstep, all that, and she’d emerged still on her feet and snarling. Oversocialized, hah. Oh, yeah, Da. I want this one.”</i>
</blockquote>It was easy to enjoy <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1106502.Komarr" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>
    <i>Komarr</i>
  </b>
</a>: Miles is one of my favourite characters and hanging out with him is delight. But Ekatarin was new to me, and although she grew on me as the book progressed, it wasn’t love at first sight. She’s complex, brave and strong by the end – but she’s timid, scared, insecure and joyless at the start. So it took me a little longer than normal to become enthralled. At one point I wondered if this might be my first <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/98254-vorkosigan-saga-chronological" rel="nofollow noopener">Vorkosigan Saga</a> to get just three-stars from me, but then it pulled round on the upward curve and thundered past the finishing line a very strong four-star rating. I finished it on my break at work today and had a big grin in the canteen – very tempting to just read straight on to the next in the series as I know my wife has bought it!<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16094.Lois_McMaster_Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">Bujold</a>’s strongest card is her characterisation, closely followed by her dialogue – and they shine as brightly as ever here. Miles case just isn’t his most fascinating and the supporting cast isn’t half as strong – no Marc, no Cordelia, no Gregor, no Ilyan, no Dendarii, etc. So <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1106502.Komarr" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>
    <i>Komarr</i>
  </b>
</a> is not my favourite of the series (that would be <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61909.Mirror_Dance" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>Mirror Dance</i>
</a>), but I still enjoyed it thoroughly and highly recommend.<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1106502.Komarr" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>
    <i>Komarr</i>
  </b>
</a> was a gift from my Grandmother-in-Law, along with two other Bujold novels she picked up for a combined price of £5 from a second-hand book stall. Thanks Nanny-B!<br><br><b>After this I read: </b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/610383596" rel="nofollow noopener">Bear's Magic Moon</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4702479664879919917" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1466752540" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1466752540" />
    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7356691-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1325898058p2/7356691.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1466752540?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky" href="/user/show/7356691-becky">Becky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1466752540" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4599950057217006956">"Is Komarr nice? It doesn't sound nice. How can a book about the son of the Butcher of Komarr being on Komarr be nice?" - literally me to my roommates before starting this book. Read that in a voice full of hurting doubt and the hopeless desire for something, not less painful, but perhaps more accessible. One grows tired of leaning back and watching Miles pull miracles out of his ass, you know. As enjoyable as that is.<br/><br/>This is the fastest I've ever gone through a Bujold book. I was LOATH to turn </span>
  <span id="freeText4599950057217006956" style="display:none">"Is Komarr nice? It doesn't sound nice. How can a book about the son of the Butcher of Komarr being on Komarr be nice?" - literally me to my roommates before starting this book. Read that in a voice full of hurting doubt and the hopeless desire for something, not less painful, but perhaps more accessible. One grows tired of leaning back and watching Miles pull miracles out of his ass, you know. As enjoyable as that is.<br /><br />This is the fastest I've ever gone through a Bujold book. I was LOATH to turn the audio book off; I could not put it down.<br /><br />This is without a doubt my favourite since Ethan and ranks right up there with Cordelia's Honor. I love this. I love Ekaterin with everything in me. I know her. Half way through this I had the horrible realization that while I want so badly to be Cordelia I might be more like Ekaterin: made small. Without a doubt, she is my greatest fear on display. Implicit in that is the very real problem with not being small: if she tries to grow, she makes the men around her small, so it's best not to even try. The perfection to which Bujold illustrates phenomena is breathtaking... it's absolutely truly staggering.<br /><br />And I adore her prose, her insight, and her turns of phrase (turns of phrases? ack). I adore Bujold's characterization. All her characters have distinct voices and I love them all.<br /><br />Kendra, or maybe it was Jas, I don't remember, said it best: it's not that Ekaterin needed a man to come and let her be big, it's just that she needed the current men in her life to get out of the way so she could do it herself. <br />All the same, I love Miles for loving her. I love HOW he loves her. I love his understanding, and I love that even if sometimes he doesn't actually understand, he's still trying to.<br />I love the whole beautiful mess and I am so, so very sad that I don't own this book.<br /><br /><br />Edit: I just re-listened to this while sick in bed, and at one point Jas came in and said, "the really frustrating part about audio books is that you've been listening to this for HOURS and he's STILL ALIVE."<br /><br />Re-listen January, 2019: I've been having a very difficult winter, and one night out of desperation for a little comfort I started listening to this one again. God I love this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4599950057217006956" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer570519902" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5634380260360584311">The wormhole plot was very interesting and satisfying, as was the full worldbuilding of Komarr itself, but what really shone brightest in the novel was Miles's falling in love with a married woman. I knew from a previous readings how important she'd become, but my goodness this was painful to watch. Delightful, absolutely, but also very painful. It was strangely believable and full of depth and realism, greatly surpassing all of his other love interests, and it really brought out the shine in hi</span>
  <span id="freeText5634380260360584311" style="display:none">The wormhole plot was very interesting and satisfying, as was the full worldbuilding of Komarr itself, but what really shone brightest in the novel was Miles's falling in love with a married woman. I knew from a previous readings how important she'd become, but my goodness this was painful to watch. Delightful, absolutely, but also very painful. It was strangely believable and full of depth and realism, greatly surpassing all of his other love interests, and it really brought out the shine in his eyes. Ill-fated love story, anyone? At least the plot actions were entirely believable and felt very natural. Their mutual discovery was slow and the tension was great, and by the end of the novel, still up in the air. As it should be.<br />To say this was a great Miles story is to say it is absolutely required reading. Like most of them. Go get them. Now. Love them. :)</span>

Miles' heart melted as well. <br/><br/><i>Komarr</i> takes place just three months after <i>Memory</i>. Miles acquires an Auditor Mentor in Ekaterin's uncle Vorthys.   <span id="freeText11951022690003765279" style="display:none">I connected deeply with the character Ekaterin. Her predicament broke my heart at times. Miles' heart melted as well. <br /><br /><i>Komarr</i> takes place just three months after <i>Memory</i>. Miles acquires an Auditor Mentor in Ekaterin's uncle Vorthys. Both Imperial Auditors arrive at Komarr to investigate a tragic and seemingly inexplicable near space accident involving an ore freighter and the Komarran solar mirror array. Each Auditor brought a different perspective and expertise to the investigation. Vorthys' engineering background appeared at first blush to be the most vital asset, but when extra parts, including body, were discovered and retrieved, Miles' unique talents became a necessity. <br /><br />Mystery, sabotage, embezzlement, get-rich-quick schemes, murder, kidnapping and revolution round out the hurdles to Miles' blossoming love life. <br /><br />Bujold keeps delivering and I keep reading. Highly recommended to space opera junkies everywhere. </span>

<div id="review_887230185" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/887230185" />
    <a title="Stuart" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9456990-stuart"><img alt="Stuart" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452041473p2/9456990.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/887230185?book_show_action=true">Jun 23, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stuart" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stuart" href="/user/show/9456990-stuart">Stuart</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9456990-stuart?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9456990-stuart?shelf=humanistic-sf">humanistic-sf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9456990-stuart?shelf=military-sf">military-sf</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer887230185" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16683579287207896700"><b>Komarr: Miles the Imperial Auditor Falls in Love</b><br/>This is probably the eighth or ninth Miles Vorkosigan novel I've listened to this year as I work my way chronologically through the series. I'm now well past the first 3-4 I read back in high school ages ago, and I can increasingly appreciate the different story arcs and overall development of Miles and the other major characters over time. Ms. Bujold has enjoyed phenomenal success with this series and an incredibly loyal fanbase thanks to her grea</span>
  <span id="freeText16683579287207896700" style="display:none"><b>Komarr: Miles the Imperial Auditor Falls in Love</b><br />This is probably the eighth or ninth Miles Vorkosigan novel I've listened to this year as I work my way chronologically through the series. I'm now well past the first 3-4 I read back in high school ages ago, and I can increasingly appreciate the different story arcs and overall development of Miles and the other major characters over time. Ms. Bujold has enjoyed phenomenal success with this series and an incredibly loyal fanbase thanks to her great skills in writing compelling, easily-accessible, enjoyable and moving space opera/mystery/adventure SF centered around incredibly real and likable characters. <br /><br />In Komarr, Miles' investigation of a mysterious space accident (or sabotage?) gets him involved in the life of an unhappily married Vor lady, Ekaterin, which becomes the main focus of the story as it progresses. Bujold deftly weaves both the Komarran conspiracy investigation with their slowly developing understanding of each other. It is not a take of romance, so much as two people learning to understand and appreciate each others' strengths and failings before it even occurs to them that they might have feelings for each other. It was handled very well indeed, and despite the lack of almost all the other fan favorite supporting cast this time around, their relationship is a fascinating and original one, especially getting to know Ekaterin and all the baggage she brings, as you wouldn't expect anyone less complex to be a match for the manic, brilliant, but vulnerable Miles Vorkosigan.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16683579287207896700" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_271667723" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/271667723" />
    <a title="Hannah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6732447-hannah"><img alt="Hannah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1575057177p2/6732447.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/271667723?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hannah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hannah" href="/user/show/6732447-hannah">Hannah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781433283215" href="/book/show/9820929-komarr">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6732447-hannah?shelf=science-fiction-futuristic">science-fiction-futuristic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6732447-hannah?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6732447-hannah?shelf=read-2012">read-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer271667723" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8481515193912419233">4.5 stars.<br/><br/><i>Komarr</i> was my second expedition into Lois McMaster Bujold's "Vorkosiverse" (my first was <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61903.Shards_of_Honour__Vorkosigan_Saga___1_' title='Shards of Honour (Vorkosigan Saga, #1) by Lois McMaster Bujold' rel='nofollow noopener'>Shards of Honour</a>), and my first introduction to Miles Vorkosigan. I have to admit that I didn't like this novel as much as <i>Shards of Honour</i>, but it had nothing to do with Miles. Miles was as wonderful as I hoped he would be. No, it was certain elements of the plot, and certain reservations about the heroine, that knocked a half-star off my rating of this otherwise brilliant novel.<br/><br/>I like to call mys</span>
  <span id="freeText8481515193912419233" style="display:none">4.5 stars.<br /><br /><i>Komarr</i> was my second expedition into Lois McMaster Bujold's "Vorkosiverse" (my first was <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61903.Shards_of_Honour__Vorkosigan_Saga___1_" title="Shards of Honour (Vorkosigan Saga, #1) by Lois McMaster Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">Shards of Honour</a>), and my first introduction to Miles Vorkosigan. I have to admit that I didn't like this novel as much as <i>Shards of Honour</i>, but it had nothing to do with Miles. Miles was as wonderful as I hoped he would be. No, it was certain elements of the plot, and certain reservations about the heroine, that knocked a half-star off my rating of this otherwise brilliant novel.<br /><br />I like to call myself a science fiction fan, but that isn't entirely accurate. The fiction part is great, but sometimes the science part kills it for me. My attention span for technical detail is extremely short, so there were sections of this novel that left me cold. These sections failed to capture my interest long enough to figure out what was going on. As a result, I had to take certain events on faith, since I hadn't paid any attention to the scientific explanations behind them. This emphasis on lengthy technical discussions instead of action sequences meant that parts of the plot lagged heavily, at least in my opinion. (I understand from my scientifically-minded <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/1478411-carrie" rel="nofollow noopener">mother</a> that this perception on my part is due to the fact that I consider math the devil and science his demonic first cousin, not due to any failings in Bujold's plot. I think she might be right, but don't tell her I said so.)<br /><br />My only other reservation about this novel was the heroine, Ekaterin. There was nothing wrong with her as a character, but her vulnerability as the subordinate partner in an unhappy marriage bothered me. I always get irritated with female characters who allow themselves to be victims. Not that Ekaterin really <i>allowed</i> herself to be a victim. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Short of killing her husband herself, I'm not sure how she could have escaped her situation earlier. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Still, she is not the partner I would have chosen for Miles.<br /><br />In all other respects, I loved <i>Komarr</i>. Bujold's writing is superb. I especially love her dialog. Her characters talk like real people do, which I appreciate after having read so much stilted dialog in other novels. I also love Bujold's ability to convey a wealth of meaning in a few short sentences. She rarely wastes much time on physical descriptions of people, places, or items, but I always have a clear picture of them in my mind. I'm looking forward to reading more of her books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8481515193912419233" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3486840895" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3486840895" />
    <a title="Lee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10818276-lee"><img alt="Lee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1341872613p2/10818276.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3486840895?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lee" href="/user/show/10818276-lee">Lee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/12779338-komarr">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=vorkosigan-series-challenge">vorkosigan-series-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=set-in-space">set-in-space</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=netgalleyreaders2020">netgalleyreaders2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=american-authors">american-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=general-fiction">general-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3486840895" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16978561134173963535">I’ve read this was not a favourite book in this series for a lot of readers; they consider it a filler or a transition book which essentially only exists to establish Miles’s new career and introduce his potential new girlfriend. I do get their point with the transition tag-I think most of the book is showing us that Miles has grown up-but, overall, Komarr has got a lot of hidden depth which they’ve failed to mention. <br/><br/>I’ve said all along that I’ve preferred the planetside mysteries with a touch </span>
  <span id="freeText16978561134173963535" style="display:none">I’ve read this was not a favourite book in this series for a lot of readers; they consider it a filler or a transition book which essentially only exists to establish Miles’s new career and introduce his potential new girlfriend. I do get their point with the transition tag-I think most of the book is showing us that Miles has grown up-but, overall, Komarr has got a lot of hidden depth which they’ve failed to mention. <br /><br />I’ve said all along that I’ve preferred the planetside mysteries with a touch of political intrigue to the space action/adventure books of the series, so Miles’s new career as an Imperial Auditor suits me just fine. I can’t quite think of an equivalent of the auditor role in real life at the moment, but I guess it’s best described as a detective with unlimited authority and resources.<br /><br />This book shows us the prejudice and bias Miles faces whilst settling into this new role. The job traditionally carries an air of respect and awe about it and auditors are automatically obeyed but, in Miles’s case, there’s the constant question of whether or not he was appointed simply due to his exalted surname. Most of his previous experience is classified and therefore, he can't reveal any details in his defence. Nevertheless, I think Young!Miles would have shown off to all and sundry without any forethought and this new mature Miles is a nice contrast, picking and choosing his moments which results in a much more effective result. (I also love how often LMB makes Miles’s past adventures amusing - his quip about being an expert when it comes to drainage and pipes, for example -- never gets old!) <br /><br />The setting for the book’s investigation is the planet Komarr of the title which also comes with an extra set of prejudices for Miles to face. His father is known to the locals as the infamous ‘butcher of Komarr’, the man they mistakenly think ordered a massacre of their peoples when the Barrayarans conquered the planet. There’re actually some really great poignant moments and brilliant quotes from Miles when he is forced to speak on behalf of his father. All in all, Miles’s behaviour in Komarr shows without doubt that he has finally become the man we all thought he’d be. <br /><br />The second point of the book is, as I said, to introduce readers to Miles’s new love interest. I was surprised that LMB actually gave us Ekaterin’s point of view (in alternate chapters with Miles’s pov). The only other time LMB has used another’s POV was in Mirror Dance (and that was Mark’s, Miles’s clone twin, whilst Miles was indisposed), so I don’t think it’s any type of spoiler to say that LMB was setting up Ekaterin as the romantic heroine for readers to cheer on. In true LMB fashion, she doesn’t make this a conventional romantic meet-cute or Ekaterin the typical female lead. <br /><br />Ekaterin is married, for starters, to a Vor administrator stationed in Komarr. She is also the niece of one of Miles’s fellow auditors and therefore, invites Miles and her uncle into her home when they come to the planet to investigate a ship’s crash, which might be an accident or might be a prelude to a terrorist act. (If you’re not such a sappy romantic as me, I promise you there’s plenty technical scifi mystery plot to keep you happy.)<br /><br />At face value, Ekaterin comes across as naive, ignorant and old fashioned, believing she must follow quite a few Vor traditions that have been left behind by most Barrayans. I was at first confused by this attitude until I realised that LMB was presenting us with a woman who is a victim of domestic abuse. No, her husband does not hit her (there’s a fabulous section featuring this thought) but she has been systematically abused by her husband for almost their entire marriage. Strong female characters are LMB’s speciality and Ekaterin’s personal journey to discovering her relationship is not normal and moving to free herself from it is wonderful. <br /><br />Miles has fallen in love several times during this series but LMB makes it pretty clear that Ekaterin is the real deal. Giving us Ekaterin’s inner thoughts, we get to learn just what she thinks of Miles and his appearance, and it’s so real and true, I just couldn’t help but fall in love with her just from that alone. <br /><br />I obviously now can’t wait for A Civil Campaign. <br /><br />5 out of 5</span>
  <a data-text-id="16978561134173963535" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/183268548" />
    <a title="Cecily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/178074-cecily"><img alt="Cecily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1327174522p2/178074.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/183268548?book_show_action=true">Jul 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cecily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cecily" href="/user/show/178074-cecily">Cecily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/178074-cecily?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/178074-cecily?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/178074-cecily?shelf=miles">miles</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer183268548" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5898351484051298918">June 2018: It's a comfort reread, everyone! Once I start, I CANNOT stop. This book is SO GOOD. My review below still stands. I mean seriously. This is one of my comfort rereads from this series now, along with Memory and Civil Campaign. And Vorpatril. And...Yeah never mind....<br/><br/>2015: I've started a wild and wacky Vorkosigan reread....backwards. It started with picking up A Civil Campaign as I often do, just to read my favorite parts (which is practically the entire book.) The events in Komarr fall</span>
  <span id="freeText5898351484051298918" style="display:none">June 2018: It's a comfort reread, everyone! Once I start, I CANNOT stop. This book is SO GOOD. My review below still stands. I mean seriously. This is one of my comfort rereads from this series now, along with Memory and Civil Campaign. And Vorpatril. And...Yeah never mind....<br /><br />2015: I've started a wild and wacky Vorkosigan reread....backwards. It started with picking up A Civil Campaign as I often do, just to read my favorite parts (which is practically the entire book.) The events in Komarr fall right before ACC and color everything so fully that I decided I wanted to reread it. It's not usually one I go back to, being one of the "Lord Auditor" Miles books that read more like really awesome whodunits rather than the military adventure form that the previous novels take. However, I've come to appreciate it for what it is: The first novel about Miles after the life-altering events in Memory (the previous novel). Miles is on a new life course and I LOVE that Komarr starts with us seeing him through the eyes of a stranger, a new character in Ekaterin. Her impressions of him post...um...everything that has happened to him in the previous couple years are quite entertaining and insightful. It's like when you run into someone who knows someone you love and haven't seen in a while. It's just fun to hear them talk about that person. It's fun to compare notes. It's fun to think about them, to see them through another's eyes...well, at least that's how I feel. (This also happens for me in Captain Vorpatril's Alliance, which is a royal kick in the pants.) <br /><br />Anyway, this novel is really Ekaterin's story. She comes to herself through various events and it's so incredibly perfect that Miles is a part of that process for her, however obliquely (or not-so-obliquely). Have I mentioned how much I love Miles? I haven't? Oh. Ok. I adore him. His presence makes any book good. I'd read about him cleaning out drainage pipes. WAIT! I've actually DONE THAT!! HAHAH! (See The Vor Game). And of course it was fantastic fun!<br /><br />Sorry, I digress. I ended up appreciating Komarr a lot more on this my...4th time through? 5th? I've lost count. I think it's partly because I'd read the following book FIRST and could see all the changes and growth the characters were about to go through. So much fun and so much cool politicking with Komarr and Barrayar.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5898351484051298918" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1266130122" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1266130122" />
    <a title="Lindsay" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10326608-lindsay"><img alt="Lindsay" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588746288p2/10326608.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1266130122?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lindsay" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lindsay" href="/user/show/10326608-lindsay">Lindsay</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10326608-lindsay?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10326608-lindsay?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1266130122" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4057304008481700277">Part of a Vorkosigan reread with the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/162270-specfic-buddy-reads' rel='nofollow noopener'>SpecFic Buddy Reads</a> group in 2017/18. I have long thought of this book as a prologue to the romantic comedy of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61899.A_Civil_Campaign__Vorkosigan_Saga___12_' title='A Civil Campaign (Vorkosigan Saga, #12) by Lois McMaster Bujold' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Civil Campaign</a>, and as such, I've not revisited it since my first reading even though I've reread A Civil Campaign multiple times. I found myself unexpectedly enjoying it for multiple reasons, partly because I misremembered it as ending with Ekaterin discovering Miles and Tien at the Waste Heat experiment station, and partly because I'd forgotten h</span>
  <span id="freeText4057304008481700277" style="display:none">Part of a Vorkosigan reread with the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/162270-specfic-buddy-reads" rel="nofollow noopener">SpecFic Buddy Reads</a> group in 2017/18. I have long thought of this book as a prologue to the romantic comedy of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61899.A_Civil_Campaign__Vorkosigan_Saga___12_" title="A Civil Campaign (Vorkosigan Saga, #12) by Lois McMaster Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">A Civil Campaign</a>, and as such, I've not revisited it since my first reading even though I've reread A Civil Campaign multiple times. I found myself unexpectedly enjoying it for multiple reasons, partly because I misremembered it as ending with Ekaterin discovering Miles and Tien at the Waste Heat experiment station, and partly because I'd forgotten how much of Miles and Ekaterin's relationship is in this novel.<br /><br />Miles is on his first official gig as an Imperial Auditor, paired with Lord Auditor Georg Vorthys to investigate the partial destruction of the Komarr soletta array, an artificial satellite solar mirror that's key part of the terraforming of Komarr. While on Komarr they stay with a local Vor administrator who is married to Vorthys's niece Ekaterin. We get Miles's viewpoint of the investigation and his attraction to Ekaterin as we also see Ekaterin's viewpoint of the final destruction of her abusive marriage and how that all ends up connecting with what's really going on.<br /><br />This is Miles at his best and being written by Bujold at the height of her ability. Miles has thoroughly grown into his abilities and life and while regretting some of his earlier mistakes, now owns them as well as his role for Barryar. For much of this book he's off balance by being forced into a reactive role, and to his credit, he recognizes that, accepts it and changes to accommodate.<br /><br />Similarly, Ekaterin is a deep and interesting character. While her marriage is horrible, she's wonderful anyway, even when she places such sharp limits around her capabilities. She's also a big part of the next two books which I'm thoroughly looking forward to.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4057304008481700277" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Oleksandr Zholud" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Oleksandr Zholud" href="/user/show/4743119-oleksandr-zholud">Oleksandr Zholud</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4743119-oleksandr-zholud?shelf=vorkosigan-1">vorkosigan-1</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3502473253" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6155594156900899367">This is the 11th novel of Vorkosigan saga, both in internal chronology and by publication date. I read is as a part of the Vorkosigan challenge in August 2020 at <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/474371-hugo-nebula-awards-best-novels' rel='nofollow noopener'>Hugo & Nebula Awards: Best Novels</a> group.<br/><br/>As we know from the previous volume, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61880.Memory__Vorkosigan_Saga___10_' title='Memory (Vorkosigan Saga, #10) by Lois McMaster Bujold' rel='nofollow noopener'>Memory</a>, Miles is no longer working for the ImpSec, instead he is ‘the voice of the emperor’, an Imperial Auditor. His first job is to find out what has happened in Komarr, where a local freighter in a strange way collided with a satellite mirror, which is impor</span>
  <span id="freeText6155594156900899367" style="display:none">This is the 11th novel of Vorkosigan saga, both in internal chronology and by publication date. I read is as a part of the Vorkosigan challenge in August 2020 at <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/474371-hugo-nebula-awards-best-novels" rel="nofollow noopener">Hugo &amp; Nebula Awards: Best Novels</a> group.<br /><br />As we know from the previous volume, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61880.Memory__Vorkosigan_Saga___10_" title="Memory (Vorkosigan Saga, #10) by Lois McMaster Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">Memory</a>, Miles is no longer working for the ImpSec, instead he is ‘the voice of the emperor’, an Imperial Auditor. His first job is to find out what has happened in Komarr, where a local freighter in a strange way collided with a satellite mirror, which is important for terraforming the planet. The case seems trivial, but the planned wedding of Emperor Gregor that ought to take place on Komarr in just a few weeks calls for a closer inspection.<br /><br />The novel is written in two POV – of Miles and of a woman from Barrayar Ekaterin Vorsoisson, whose unhappy marriage made her hide all her feelings behind an icy façade, for both her husband and her son have a serious inherited disease, which starts affecting people’s behavior in their 30s or later and we all know how Barrayaran feel about weak or ill. Of course, Miles fells in love with her…<br /><br />A nice continuation of the series, with a change of gears and a mystery and a tragic love story instead of daring escapades of younger Miles.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1942919849" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1942919849" />
    <a title="Lilia Ford" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10992009-lilia-ford"><img alt="Lilia Ford" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1381027796p2/10992009.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1942919849?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lilia Ford" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lilia Ford" href="/user/show/10992009-lilia-ford">Lilia Ford</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1942919849" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17618387714255039544">3.5<br/><br/>This is quite different from any of the other books in the series: the picture of a failing marriage is bleak and uncompromising and utterly realistic. It verges on depressing but the character work is truly impressive. This really is Ekaterin's story, however, and there's not too much development for Miles. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Weirdly the only lightness comes from the scenes with the terrorists, who are mostly academics and engineers and as far as possible from the usual "fanatic" cliches about t</span></span>
  <span id="freeText17618387714255039544" style="display:none">3.5<br /><br />This is quite different from any of the other books in the series: the picture of a failing marriage is bleak and uncompromising and utterly realistic. It verges on depressing but the character work is truly impressive. This really is Ekaterin's story, however, and there's not too much development for Miles. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Weirdly the only lightness comes from the scenes with the terrorists, who are mostly academics and engineers and as far as possible from the usual "fanatic" cliches about terrorists. I really respected that Bujold never lost sight of their humanity even while giving an unforgiving picture of the devastation that would result from their plan.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />Bottom line: This book will never be a favorite, but it's not a bad read by any means and it introduces a major new character, Ekaterin, who will play a key role in Miles' life going forward. </span>

<div id="review_239402752" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/239402752" />
    <a title="Althea Ann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3846743-althea-ann"><img alt="Althea Ann" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411566466p2/3846743.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Althea Ann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Althea Ann" href="/user/show/3846743-althea-ann">Althea Ann</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer239402752" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4400366617305078272">Following directly upon the events of 'Memory,' 'Komarr' still functions as a stand-alone novel.<br/><br/>And... I liked it even better than 'Memory.' The plot felt more original, and it just has a really well-structured, exciting story, backed up by well-rounded, believable characters and a vivid, consistent setting.<br/><br/>Miles Vorkosigan is sent, in his role as Imperial Auditor to the still-somewhat-rebellious subject planet of Komarr to investigate a space accident (or, possibly, act of sabotage) that may se</span>
  <span id="freeText4400366617305078272" style="display:none">Following directly upon the events of 'Memory,' 'Komarr' still functions as a stand-alone novel.<br /><br />And... I liked it even better than 'Memory.' The plot felt more original, and it just has a really well-structured, exciting story, backed up by well-rounded, believable characters and a vivid, consistent setting.<br /><br />Miles Vorkosigan is sent, in his role as Imperial Auditor to the still-somewhat-rebellious subject planet of Komarr to investigate a space accident (or, possibly, act of sabotage) that may seriously impact Komarr's terraforming project.<br /><br />He accepts the hospitality of his colleague's niece, whose husband happens to be an administrator in that terraforming project. Unfortunately, the husband's also a shiftless jerk, and his and Ekaterin's marriage is on the verge of falling apart. <br /><br />As layers of plots and motivations unravel, you'll find yourself staying up late to finish... well, at least I did!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4400366617305078272" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1648789980" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12009587024564628643">So good. I loved getting to see Miles through someone else's eyes. This one alternates perspectives between Ekaterin and Miles. Ekaterin is awesome. I was so worried about whether or not I'd like her because I haven't loved any of Miles' other love interests. I shouldn't have worried. Bujold is a sorceress. I loved watching Miles fall for her (He falls in love fast and hard. I love Miles.). The last 40 pages or so were so much fun. The climactic scene, Ekaterin's reaction to being "rescued", the</span>
  <span id="freeText12009587024564628643" style="display:none">So good. I loved getting to see Miles through someone else's eyes. This one alternates perspectives between Ekaterin and Miles. Ekaterin is awesome. I was so worried about whether or not I'd like her because I haven't loved any of Miles' other love interests. I shouldn't have worried. Bujold is a sorceress. I loved watching Miles fall for her (He falls in love fast and hard. I love Miles.). The last 40 pages or so were so much fun. The climactic scene, Ekaterin's reaction to being "rescued", the open flirtation of the final conversation between the two of them in the last chapter (That escalated quickly! :) )...just wonderful. I'm running out of adjectives to describe how much I'm loving this series. :)</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20233424-joanka?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20233424-joanka?shelf=usa">usa</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2599063237" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16656414139481481870">What a delightful come back to the Vorkosigan saga it was! I loved the new character, Ekaterin and she touched me deeply on many levels. The plot was interesting enough so as to make a nice background, additionally showing some more of the whole Bujold universe and I admire her world a lot. But, as usually, what I loved the most was the psyhological portrait of the main characters, with all their flaws, vices, shortcomings and wonderful virtues. It's so easy to get engaged in Bujold's characters</span>
  <span id="freeText16656414139481481870" style="display:none">What a delightful come back to the Vorkosigan saga it was! I loved the new character, Ekaterin and she touched me deeply on many levels. The plot was interesting enough so as to make a nice background, additionally showing some more of the whole Bujold universe and I admire her world a lot. But, as usually, what I loved the most was the psyhological portrait of the main characters, with all their flaws, vices, shortcomings and wonderful virtues. It's so easy to get engaged in Bujold's characters, they become so fast important to me that I can't stop reading. This time it was also the case. I found Ekaterin's story sad but also strangely soothing and empowering. If you come to this volume from the start believe me, you are in for a treat.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16656414139481481870" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('VHorRsdG9NWfbRIPPJR0+P2ewKgYogmMqRX8KCxIQDAhSv+jaLvNEj/8m3djy1JOclzUeg7mR8ZYJn3v7D+VqQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

That was the setting when Tailyn was again placed on the road to uncertainty, beset by terrifying lixes, and hounded by a harsh trainer it was impossible to please. All he can do is bear up and keep pushing forward in the hopes that his wishes will be granted. As legend has it, somewhere ahead lies the Forest of Desire, a place capable of bringing to life one’s every wish. For example, returning Valia Levor, Tailyn’s betrothed, who was kidnapped. <span id="freeTextContainer5740980523688811185">Lois McMaster Bujold was born in 1949, the daughter of an engineering professor at Ohio State University, from whom she picked up her early interest in science fiction. She now lives in Minneapolis, and has two grown children. <br/><br/>Her fantasy from HarperCollins includes the award-winning Chalion series and the Sharing Knife tetralogy; her science fiction from Baen Books features the perennially bestse</span>
  <span id="freeText5740980523688811185" style="display:none">Lois McMaster Bujold was born in 1949, the daughter of an engineering professor at Ohio State University, from whom she picked up her early interest in science fiction. She now lives in Minneapolis, and has two grown children. <br /><br />Her fantasy from HarperCollins includes the award-winning Chalion series and the Sharing Knife tetralogy; her science fiction from Baen Books features the perennially bestselling Vorkosigan Saga. Her work has been translated into over twenty languages.<br /><br />A listing of her awards and nominations may be seen here:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.sfadb.com/Lois_McMaster_Bujold">http://www.sfadb.com/Lois_McMaster_Bu...</a><br /> <br />A listing of her interviews is here:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://vorkosigan.wikia.com/wiki/Author_Interviews">http://vorkosigan.wikia.com/wiki/Auth...</a><br /><br />An older fan-run site devoted to her work, The Bujold Nexus, is here:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.dendarii.com/">http://www.dendarii.com/</a><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

</script>
